I have played and thoroughly enjoyed games such as the Souls-games (Sekiro included) and am now looking for another game that has the best combat out there! I like harder games with smooth-feeling combat, where the story is not as important to me as how polished the combat is. I am mainly looking for a melee-combat type of game, so no shooter recommendations. Anime is something I love so good anime games are always welcome recommendations too!
Ghost Of Tsushima had pretty decent combat.
It's sad how the enemy variety is so limited, but your combat options and the general feel are a blast indeed.
Devil May Cry series has my favorite melee combat. Maybe not as hard as souls but really fun.
Also heard good things about Nioh, tho I haven't played it myself.
Nioh 2 probably has the best souls-like combat outside of Sekiro. A lot of action adventure games have really good combat if you dedicate time like Sifu, Devil May Cry 5 and Bayonetta 3.
If you like mech stuff, Armored Core 6 combat is pretty incredible, very smooth and flashy.
Amazing combat combined with the nemesis system and the fighting pits is such a rewarding experience I've not been able to replicate elsewhere.
I‚Äôll always respect that the devs made a combat system make you feel overpowered but still challenging and actually difficult.
I'm gonna be honest, Sekiro probably has the smoothest melee combat to date. But a game that I've been enjoying recently with smooth combat is DMC5. There is something fun about extending your combos and just learning the overall mechanics.
Devil may cry 5 is the pinnacle of the games with great combat
The Bayonetta has quite a deep combat system with a huge moveset
Play both of the god of war games on their hardest difficulties, super satisfying and visually impressive combat
Wanted: dead (melee/shooter hybrid but it‚Äôs sekiro melee combat)
Scarlet nexus. It‚Äôs a bit of a DMC clone but it all comes to better with tons of powers and will have you feeling like a god by the end of it. Easy rec especially if you like anime. Hell all these recs are good if you like anime
Since Arkham was mentioned, I‚Äôll also throw in Shadow of Mordor (and Shadow of War), since it has a similar combat system
I personally liked the combat of Jedi: Fallen Order
Dragons Dogma has the best combat in any action RPG. Imagine a mix between Monster Hunter and Dark Souls, with faster melee combat.
There's a lot that's great about Nier Automata but the combat isn't. It's not bad but nothing special either, definitely a lot weaker than some other Platinum titles like Vanquish or MGRising.
Nioh 2 is by far one of the most rewarding combat systems once you get going with it. Totally recommended if you haven't.
Armored Core 6, nothing else like it, pretty easy too.
DmC: Devil May Cry and Devil May Cry 5. Creme de la creme when it comes to combat systems. DmC has a stupid (still fun) story and awesome combat but has some platforming. DMC5 is just ü§åüèªü§åüèª. Great story, fun characters, incredible combat. Level Design is meh but still one of the best combat systems, if not the best, after Sekiro.

G2A.COM G2A News Features Games with Best Combat
Most games feature some degree of combat.
Sometimes it‚Äôs extremely abstracted and simplified, other times it‚Äôs the main focus. In this list we‚Äôre taking a look at the latter: we‚Äôre here to bring to your attention games which have tight, polished, exciting combat systems. Most are melee-focused action games, but there are a few surprises which break this trend, but still very much qualify.
Some of these systems will be complex, others will be relatively simple, but responsive and impactful. Other still may be amazing by their tactical depth or sheer fun factor. The one thing that unifies them is the joy and satisfaction you get out of them once you master the skills necessary to turn into an engine of destruction.
Its recent arrival on PC is a great excuse to put Ghost Tsushima on the list of the best combat sytems in video games.
Most of the system revolves around swordsmanship, with the family katana as the primary weapon, but there‚Äôs also a bow and smaller gadgets like thrown kunai or distracting firecrackers. Blended together, they give the protagonist, Jin Sakai, a range of tactical options for any situation.
Swordfighting is governed by four stances effective against specific enemy types, and coming with their own special attacks. Beyond these forms, the system heavily features dodges and parrying, including perfect variants which might even trigger unique mechanical effects. Combined with high lethality, combat in GoT is tense, fast, and satisfying, complementing the game‚Äôs themes and story.
Excellent third-person melee-first action game
Stealth is a valuable tool, and is sometimes the preferred approach
Sifu is an absolute treat for enthusiasts of unarmed martial arts.
This third-person action game goes to great lengths to present a believable and realistic depiction of a style closely related to Bak Mei kung fu. The system takes some time to learn, but when you do, the flurry of dodges, blocks, whip-fast strikes and crowd-controlling holds looks and feels incredible to unleash.
Over time you‚Äôll learn additional maneuvers, learn how to better utilize improvised staffs or loose pipes, letting you knock out goons and elites as if you were an incarnation of Bruce Lee himself. The game has several stages, each following a different theme, and culminating in a boss fight which is perfectly easy to pass‚Ä¶ as long as you have mastered your basics. It‚Äôs that kind of game.
When you die, you get a few years older‚Ä¶ can you beat the final boss before getting too old?
Incredible animations and responsive controls
A challenge mode for people who crave more combat
Scarlet Nexus flew a bit under the radar when it launched in 2021, despite its obvious quality.
It‚Äôs an action RPG from Bandai Namco, which makes it a cousing to Code Vein and Tales of Arise. It‚Äôs a strong competition, and Scralt Nexus is keen to meet it fair and square with a sword and impressive telekinetic abilities, which turn the environments into, essential an arsenal of improvised weapons.
What‚Äôs important, is that stringing a random debris toss into your combos feels smooth and convenient. Swordfighting itself also feels great, and through SN‚Äôs dual protagonists you‚Äôll experience two different playstyles. Yuito focuses on using a katana first, telekinesis second, while his counterpart, Kasane, prefers ranged combat with a stronger focus on TK and helpful throwing knives.
Excellent, telekinetically enhanced combat
The enemies you fight have excelent, freaky designs
Warhammer: Vermintide 2 take s a combined arms approach, in that it won‚Äôt take long before the ground will be littered with the combines arms of Chaos worshippers and Skaven.
Jokes aside, combat in Vermintide 2 isn‚Äôt ass deep as in other games here, but it‚Äôs incredibly satisfying anyway, and feels fantastically tactile when you slice through a swarming horde of humanoid rats.
Each weapon has its own specific traits, some having substantial buffs to defense, others capable of cleaving through multiple enemies, etc. These attributes make a big difference in how the given character is going to fight even withing a single career. An Ironbreaker fielding Hammer and Shield with Drakefire Pistols will be very different from one using A War Pick with a Handgun, for example.
5 playable characters, each with four very different careers
Intense first-person melee and range combat
A ton of weapon types and an upgrade system to make them stronger
More story-driven than you‚Äôd expect it to be
Hi-Fi Rush was a sneaky hit of 2023, a character-action game taking the best lessons from the likes of Devil May Cry, but mixing them with‚Ä¶ a rhythm game.
For plot reasons, the entire world of the game obeys the same rhythm. Platforms move to the beat, enemies‚Äô attacks are timed accordingly, and your own strikes are much stronger if you can sync with the music. It creates a fascinating mix.
When you figure out the timing, you know when you‚Äôre going to be hit, giving you an edge for dodging and parrying. When you know the beat, you know how to maximise your damage and possibly unleash an extra-powerful special or a team-up move. Attaining a state of flow in Hi-Fi Rush feels incredibly satisfying, especially since the game‚Äôs aesthetic and animations make it vibrant and lively.
Mixing melee combat with a rhythm game was a match made in heaven
Excellent, cartoonish, cel shaded art style and designs
Developed by studio behind The Evil Within and Ghostwire: Tokyo
Jedi Survivor built very competently on the foundations established by its predecessor, Jedi: Fallen Order.
In terms of combat, which interests us here and now, it deepened and expanded the combat styles. Each of the three forms from JFO (single blade, two sword, double-bladed sword) received a dedicated progression trees, and we got two more styles on top of those.
The new styles are an interesting mix sword and blaster combo giving you impressive ranged option with customizable special shots, and a two-handed form which is slow, but hits like a ton of bricks. You can have two styles equipped simultaneously, switching between them with a button, which makes you much more responsive in combat and encourages mastering several playstyles.
Five fully developed forms of lightsaber, including an odd but cool Sword and Blaster
Drastically improved movement options, including a grappling hook
Many fantastic, thrilling scripted sequences, this time with way fewer slides
A fun hub for the story: a cantina on a remote planet
The full release of Baldur‚Äôs Gate 3 was a momentous even for gaming, and cemented Larian‚Äôs game among the genre‚Äôs best.
It doesn‚Äôt have dynamic sword fighting or anything of the sort, but its turn-based combat is excellent for the task of making you feel like you can do anything. Toss an exploding barrel, throw an enemy off a cliff, or turn into a massive beast and dropkick people to death‚Ä¶
With twelve distinct classes, each with several subclasses, a complex system of actions and reactions, powerful abilities, and a reactive environment, fights in BG3 are impressively tactile. The reason you might have not heard of all that, is because the community discussions focus a lot more on the dramatic, well-written, cinematically presented and incredibly reactive story. Truly, a cRPG for the ages.
A lot of fun tools to define your build‚Ä¶ and an easy respect if you mess up
The battlefields are hardly ever static, something weird is always likely to happen
One of the unquestionable hits of 2023 and the genre in general
Many different endings, including a few for the most villainous of you
It‚Äôs not unusual for Devil May Cry games to have multiple playable characters.
What is somewhat unusual is to make them central to the game and THAT different in playstyle. In DMC5 we‚Äôve got weapon-juggling Dante whose combos looks like a flurry of weapon swaps, Nero, who‚Äôs committed to his sword and gun, but has a gallery of cool prosthetic arms with various powers, and then there‚Äôs V.
V is an odd one, because this fellow is rather un-athletic and vulnerable, so instead of weapons he uses summoned creatures: a raven, a panther, and a goliath, all with their own range of attacks and abilities you can deploy. Oh, and of course there‚Äôs also a Vergil DLC. Truly, DMC5 is a treat for any fan of figuring out ridiculous combos and playstyle diversity.
Three playable characters in the core game, each with a very different style
The peak of DMC gameplay complexity, but it‚Äôs not inaccessible to newcomers
The better you play, the richer the soundtrack
Many years after the original came Dragon‚Äôs Dogma 2, and it brought with it a lot of new things to enjoy.
In addition to a fresh world to save, it also brought back the original‚Äôs juicy combat system, now best experienced through ten vastly different vocations AKA classes. There are classics like a sword-and-shield fighter or a support mage‚Ä¶ but there‚Äôs also Warfarer, the star of the game.
Warfarer is a vocation which can use every other vocation‚Äôs armor, weapons, and abilities, letting you assemble your own unique playstyle. The trick is that you have to switch active weapons to use associated skills, and you have to predefine the rotation. It takes some planning, and a lot of skill to use it effectively, but when you do it‚Äôs where DD2‚Äôs combat system becomes absolutely brilliant.
Ten distinct vocations, including one built for multiclassing
A large world which never lacks in enemies to climb onto and stab in the‚Ä¶ eye
Your NPC companions, Pawns, are plugging the gaps in your offense and defense alike
Surrounded by a list of sword masters of all sorts, Titanfall 2 nevertheless deserves a spot, because it does all sorts of cool things about its shooting.
It comes mostly through the exceptional mobility, which allows you to run circles around you enemies and attack them from unexpected angles. The tutorial alone teaches you to shoot and throw grenades while wall-running and sliding.
Before long you‚Äôll also gain access to a Titan, a hulking mech/robot with its own growing selection of abilities. Shields which allow you to throw bullets back at you enemies, flamethrowers, swords, there‚Äôs a loadout for every situation. Jumping into the fray in Titanfall 2 is exciting every time, and once you score three headshots while wall-running you won‚Äôt want to go back to earth-bound shooters.
A perfect mix of parkour and deadly firepower
You also get to stomp around in a big mech
With practice you‚Äôll fluidly slide and wall-run from enemy to enemy
Mordhau is a treat for any enthusiast of medieval armed combat. And unarmed too, if you‚Äôre determined enough.
The game features an impressive arsenal of weapons and armor you can equip to battle, limited mostly by the very sensible points system. Once you‚Äôre on the battlefield, that‚Äôs when the fun begins. There are plenty of maneuvers you can perform, including the titular Mordhau.
Each weapon handles differently, each armor has its benefits and drawbacks (like speed penalties), and while the fights tend to be quite hectic, there is a lot of room for technique and skill to shine. Dodging blows, parrying, even mounted combat are all in there. Techniques are more about spur of the moment decision than deploying specific combos, but that just adds to the realism.
One of the most realistic PvP melee combat simulators
Chivalry 2 functions in a similar space as Mordhau: an online multiplayer game focus on melee PvP.
It doesn‚Äôt go too far into simulation, settling for three attack paths (two slashes and a stab) which you can chain together smoothly. On the defensive side, you can, of course, block attacks, and a well-times parry can stagger your attacker, opening them up for a counterstrike.
A neat thing is that if you happen to sever an enemy‚Äôs limb you can pick it up and clobber the next opponent with it. On top of individual combat, you can also get behind a ballista, or join other players in a siege. Battles can get quite large, with up 64 players supported. You‚Äôll always have plenty of opponents but be careful where you swing your weapons: friendly fire is a thing.
Relatively simple, but fast and satisfying combat system
Several maps and three core modes: Free-for-All, Team Objective, and Team Deathmatch
After Dark Souls and Bloodborne, the famous FromSoftware studio decided to make something familiar, but a bit different.
See, in Sekiro: Shadows Die Twice the default way to win a fight isn‚Äôt to whittle the healthbar down to zero. Instead, if you can throw the enemy off-balance they‚Äôll be open for a lethal blow, ending most fights immediately. The thing is‚Ä¶you need good timing for that.
To do that, you need to fill the opponent‚Äôs Posture bar, but perfect parries or special dodges will help you along. Timing is absolutely crucial in Sekiro, but, thankfully, you also have a number of ninja gadgets which can help you tremendously. Sekiro‚Äôs combat is fast, precise, leaves little room for blunders, but when you perfectly parry a boss‚Äô barrage of blows, it feels amazing.
Set in a fantastical version of a Sengoku period Japan
Beautiful and well-designed levels and encounters
Created by the developers of the Ninja Gaiden series, Nioh can draw on years of experience to deliver an excellent and varied action game.
Where Sekiro focused on a single weapon, the katana, Nioh takes a broader approach, and lets players pick and choose from a broad arsenal of weapons, all of which have their own progression independent from your character‚Äôs William Adams.
In addition to the multitude of weapons, you also need to consider the three stances you can assume in combat, the aggressive high stance, balanced medium stance, and defensive low stance. Add to THAT Ki management techniques and you get an action game with a combat system with plenty of depth and breadth. Choose your weapon, master your skills, and complete William‚Äôs vendetta.
You can read our comparison between Sekiro and Nioh
Inspired by the history of a real-life Irish samurai
Several weapon types, three stances, plenty of skills to master
A combat system doesn‚Äôt need to be incredibly complex or realistic to be awesome. Hollow Knight is a great example of that.
Its combat system is fast, responsive, and features special ‚ÄúNail Art‚Äù abilities to use in conjunction with the basic dashes, strikes, and jumps. And you will need to get the hang of them all, because the boss fights don‚Äôt mess around and require focus and concentration.
Oh, in addition to Nail Arts you ALSO get spells which cost Soul but their effects are worth the price. Once you get all the abilities, the boss fights turn into a flurry of well-timed dashes, exploding spells, and quick strikes. Hollow Knight is rightfully held as one of the best Metroidvanias currently on the market, and one of the best-animated 2D games you can play right now.
Bulletstorm wants nothing more than to give you the tools and motivation to be as creative with its guns as you could possibly be.
It accomplished that through Skillshot system, which awards you points for‚Ä¶almost everything that isn‚Äôt just boring shooting. It ranges from targeting specific body parts to using alternate fire modes to accomplish some highly specific things.
And you can combo all of that! Sending your enemy into the air, setting them on fire, leashing them back down you just so you can kick them into a cactus is a thing you can do, and the game wants you to be even MORE elaborate. All for the sweet, sweet points you can then use for (special) ammo and upgrades. Furthermore, the Skillshots also have delightfully silly names, which is a big plus.
The Skillshot system does a great job motivating you to get creative
Eight cool guns with explosive alternate fire modes
Monster Hunter: World already has a great, deep combat system, featuring 14 weapons with unique moves and qualities.
Even weapons which might seem similar, like greatsword and longsword function in fundamentally different ways, and that‚Äôs not even getting to odd weapons such as a charge blade or the hunting horn. And then the Iceborne expansion came and added a new bunch of new stuff.
In addition to a whole new world to monsterhunt in, Iceborne introduced the clutch claw. With this buffed up grappling hook you can dish out some damage or steer a monster towards a wall. There are also new weapon-specific moves worth adding to the usual move flow, not only because they are very useful, but also because they look pretty damn cool, which is nothing to sneeze at.
14 weapon types, all with unique move sets
Excellent boss fights and creative monster designs
Strong emphasis on assembling a proper loadout for the hunts
Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance, produced by the creators of hits like NieR: Automata and Bayonetta.
Platinum Games, is a pretty interesting game, really. With the cyberninja Raiden as its protagonist, it has a perfectly functional core combat system, but what gets it the spot on this list is the Blade Mode, AKA ‚ÄúCut Everything‚Äù AKA ‚ÄúOh dear lord, so detailed‚Äù.
If something has a discrete model, then there is 95% chance you‚Äôll be able to cut it to tiny pieces. If you‚Äôre determined enough, you can cut a watermelon down to party-appropriate pieces. The game launched in 2013 (where did the time go?) and yet nobody seems eager to do something similar. We do have dismemberment in many games, of course, but nothing near the freeform of Revengeance.
Features Raiden, whom you might know from other Metal Gear games
Dark Messiah is a spin-off from the Might and Magic series, a first-person perspective shooter/slasher with deliciously meaty combat and its systems were full of kinetic joy.
If you pick melee combat as your focus, you‚Äôll find yourself hacking orcs to pieces with swords, whacking them around with staves, and every hit and every parry feels like it has proper weight behind it.
If that‚Äôs not enough to provide a nice immersion, you quickly discover the joys of ragdolling enemies with well-aimed kicks, swinging chandeliers, or falling barrels. If you‚Äôre tactical enough, you‚Äôll impale your foes on spikes abundant in the game‚Äôs environments. Magic works like wonder, too, with a level of interactivity unseen until Divinity: Original Sin (and its successors) decided to make it one of its core features.
You can use the environment to your advantage
Mount & Blade: Warband is a very good for for this list mostly because of its massive variety of melee weapons.
Each of them has its own stats you need to consider: things like speed rating or separate damage values for each attack type. Some weapons even have different modes (e.g. you can use a bastard sword one-handed or two-handed), or special properties, like punching through parries.
You control the type of attack with mouse movement and parrying is managed in the same way. Momentum has importance too, especially if you grab a lance and choose to kill someone from horseback. The game isn‚Äôt pretty, true, but the combat and battles are a ton of fun, and every weapon feels unique.
UPDATE: The sequel, Bannerlord, launched in 2020, improved on virtually everything.
A sandbox experience in a medieval-like world
Plenty of realistic weapons, both ranged and melee
Yeah, we had the Force Unleashed series, which made lightsaber combat look cool, but it never managed to make lightsaber feel cool.
This is where the Jedi Knight games come in. First with Jedi Outcast II, specifically, and then in Jedi Academy, which added a few very welcome features and extra variety to the gameplay.
Running around slashing foes, directing attacks with subtle movements of your mouse buttons and pre-determined maneuvers was a blast, especially with Raven Software‚Äôs dismemberment engine. Jedi Academy added dual lightsabers, and Darth Maul-like staves, each with unique movesets, of course. Buff it all up with acrobatics, and The Force Unleashed can hide.
Kyle Katarn is awesome both as a protagonist and as a mentor
Jedi Academy features dual lightsabers and double-bladed lightsaber
Keeping up the theme of abnormally fast games with absurd skill ceiling, let‚Äôs talk Guilty Gear.
The decades-old franchise is in some ways a fighting game version of Devil May Cry. Although it has entered the 3D world with the release of Xrd, it lost none of the speed and crispness of the previous, sprite-based incarnations.
There‚Äôs all the complexity expected from fighting games, with cancels, five types of attacks, specials, and more. GG‚Äôs systems are complex and require split-second reaction speed, which make it less friendly to newcomers, but very satisfying once you get the hang of them. Oh, and the soundtracks are some prime-quality hard rock, as befits the franchise so heavily inspired by rock history.
Looks fantastic, but has a very pronounced anime aesthetic
At its core, For Honor‚Äôs system unitially seems to boil down to picking one of three directions: top, left, or right. If your enemy matches the direction of their guard to your attack, it‚Äôs blocked.
Then you add fast and heavy attacks, specific moves of the various and numerous classes‚Ä¶
Before long you figure out that what looks like a fairly simple rock-paper-scissors type of deal gets enough modifiers and complexities to turn it into a competent, deep 3D fighting game. There are several modes to check out, plenty of classes from several factions, and a lot of customization options to unlock, because looking good on a field of battle is important.
Tekken 8 being playable on PC is a cause for celebration already. It also happens to be a pretty darned nifty fighting game, perfecting the more than 20 years old system, and pushing it to the logical conclusion.
This is what a long time of ‚Äútesting‚Äù in Japanese arcades does to games, it seems. Tekken at its core is focused on controlling individual limbs, chaining attacks, and looking great.
It‚Äôs probably among the smoothest fighting games out there, system and animation-wise. The hitboxes are also very detailed, which can lead to some amazing replays. Tekken might not be the most complex of them all, but polish and cutting away things which do not work is also an important part of development. And Tekken is great at this.
Precise martial art-focused fighting game
Represents many different fighting styles
The presence of this series is probably no surprise to anyone here. Soulsbornes have become something of a measuring stick for many people.
The games have a certainly demanding combat system, which is typically reasonably fair, but also knows no mercy. The key to victory lies in managing your stamina, which is drained by‚Ä¶everything, and in learning your enemies‚Äô attack patterns.
Working out the proper timing to attack, block, dodge will hopefully keep you beyond the striking range of your opponents. It‚Äôs a series of games with a very deliberate tempo, nothing like DMC‚Äôs mad speed. The always present threat of violent death, and combat system unlike many we‚Äôve seen before all put From Software‚Äôs games as the shining example of how to do challenging combat in games, for better or worse.
Patience is rewarded, as is learning your enemies‚Äô moves
Many different weapon types from which you can choose your favorite
So there you have it. Twenty games with good combat systems. Some require skill and patience to master, others are simpler, but with a large scope, or offering excellent interactivity. We‚Äôve even found room for turn-based Baldur‚Äôs Gate 3, and two dedicated shooters.
However, you can‚Äôt ‚Äútry again‚Äù until you take the first step, so head on yonder to our marketplace and grab the game which sounds like the most fun, considering your preferences. You‚Äôre bound to find attractive deals which will sweeten the experience.

Sign in to your Game Rant account Summary Red Dead Redemption 2 offers precise and advanced combat with the Dead Eye system. Metal Gear Solid 5 features engaging combat encounters that feel natural and unpredictable. Fallout 4 provides chaotic shooting scenes and utilizes the VATs system for targeting specific enemy parts. The open-world video game genre has become one of the staples of the industry. These huge, expansive worlds have left players in awe for decades. And within the scope of unlimited possibilities and things to do within these worlds, some of them have also created deep, complex combat systems that allow players to feel powerful in a hostile and aggressive world. These games have found ways to infuse incredible combat into huge worlds, a task that has proven rather difficult over the years due to the unpredictability of the player's involvement. Some of these games have focused combat encounters around melee and magic, while others see players engaging enemies with firearms and tactical espionage. Whatever route a game takes, these titles have done so with precision, crafting the best combat systems in the open-world genre. These open-world games have been ranked based on their battle systems, and how well the combat encounters are woven into the environments. Posts 1 By Alex Daniel Reid May 4, 2025 7 Red Dead Redemption 2 Use Dead Eye To Eliminate Enemies Red Dead Redemption 2 10/10 Released October 26, 2018 Where to play Close WHERE TO PLAY DIGITAL PHYSICAL ESRB M for Mature: Blood and Gore, Intense Violence, Nudity, Sexual Content, Strong Language, Use of Drugs and Alcohol Developer(s) Rockstar Games Genre(s) Action, Adventure Powered by Expand Collapse Rockstar's open-world Wild West epic began in 2003 when they purchased the rights to the Red Dead IP from Capcom, which led to the franchise becoming one of the cornerstones of the company. While the original Red Dead Redemption was an instant classic when it launched in 2010, Rockstar produced a prequel in 2018 that took everything about the first game and improved on it, including the already compelling combat. Much like the first game, Red Dead Redemption 2 uses the Dead Eye system, which allows the player to lock onto enemies and slow down time in order to mark enemies for execution. Thanks to the improvements in hardware after RDR1, the prequel features a much more dynamic, free-flowing version of Dead Eye that also utilizes advanced gore to sell the harsh reality of the Old West. Shooting in Red Dead Redemption 2 feels precise and snappy, and is easily Rockstar's most accomplished combat system. 6 Metal Gear Solid 5: The Phantom Pain The Franchise's Most Complete Combat System Metal Gear Solid 5 The Phantom Pain 9/10 Released September 1, 2015 Where to play Close WHERE TO PLAY DIGITAL PHYSICAL ESRB m Developer(s) Konami, Kojima Productions Genre(s) Stealth, Action-Adventure, Shooter, Adventure Powered by Expand Collapse Metal Gear creator Hideo Kojima continued to expand the combat possibilities of the franchise with Snake Eater and Guns of the Patriots. However, the most refined version of the series' combat system was released in 2015 with The Phantom Pain. Utilizing nearly every aspect of prior combat systems, Kojima and his team crafted a unique, engaging world. Encounters feel natural and are treated with an unpredictability that makes each one more exciting than the last. Posts By Maddie Fisher May 18, 2025 After setting the stage with Ground Zeroes, a prologue released a little over a year prior to the launch of The Phantom Pain, the team at Kojima Productions crafted what is still one of the most incredible examples of an open-world stealth game ever made. The open-world video game genre has become one of the staples of the industry. These huge, expansive worlds have left players in awe for decades. And within the scope of unlimited possibilities and things to do within these worlds, some of them have also created deep, complex combat systems that allow players to feel powerful in a hostile and aggressive world. These games have found ways to infuse incredible combat into huge worlds, a task that has proven rather difficult over the years due to the unpredictability of the player's involvement.
Some of these games have focused combat encounters around melee and magic, while others see players engaging enemies with firearms and tactical espionage. Whatever route a game takes, these titles have done so with precision, crafting the best combat systems in the open-world genre. These open-world games have been ranked based on their battle systems, and how well the combat encounters are woven into the environments.
Open-world games are the shining star of the gaming industry. Of the many settings found within this genre, these are the most timeless and iconic.
Rockstar's open-world Wild West epic began in 2003 when they purchased the rights to the Red Dead IP from Capcom, which led to the franchise becoming one of the cornerstones of the company. While the original Red Dead Redemption was an instant classic when it launched in 2010, Rockstar produced a prequel in 2018 that took everything about the first game and improved on it, including the already compelling combat.
Much like the first game, Red Dead Redemption 2 uses the Dead Eye system, which allows the player to lock onto enemies and slow down time in order to mark enemies for execution. Thanks to the improvements in hardware after RDR1, the prequel features a much more dynamic, free-flowing version of Dead Eye that also utilizes advanced gore to sell the harsh reality of the Old West. Shooting in Red Dead Redemption 2 feels precise and snappy, and is easily Rockstar's most accomplished combat system.
The Franchise's Most Complete Combat System
Metal Gear creator Hideo Kojima continued to expand the combat possibilities of the franchise with Snake Eater and Guns of the Patriots. However, the most refined version of the series' combat system was released in 2015 with The Phantom Pain. Utilizing nearly every aspect of prior combat systems, Kojima and his team crafted a unique, engaging world. Encounters feel natural and are treated with an unpredictability that makes each one more exciting than the last.
5 Metal Gear Environments Based On Real World Locations

The Phantom Pain also offers a wide variety of tools and abilities that Snake can use during combat. The act of marking a base for infiltration, then raiding it, is one of the most addictive game feels of the last generation. However, the answer to this question is very much dependent on a player's individual tastes. Any of the games on our best story games list could qualify depending on your taste in genre and storytelling style. If you're a fan of more realistic tales, you're more likely to get a kick out of Red Dead Redemption 2 than the more fanciful Baldur's Gate 3. That being said, sometimes stepping out of your comfort zone can be rewarding, as you may discover a brand-new type of game that you may never have considered before. For instance, though Deus Ex may be unfamiliar to many on account of its age, the sci-fi classic is well worth a look.What is the best story game right now?Between Clair Obscur: Expedition 33 and Assassin's Creed Shadows, story fans are eating well at the moment. However, it's hard to say which story game is the absolute 'best'. Personal taste is a huge factor in determining which games stick with us and, while every title on this best story games list is a masterclass in its own right, we can't rightly say that any one of them stands above the others. That said, if you're interested in seeing how modern game development tackles story games, then the aforementioned Baldur's Gate 3 and Final Fantasy 7 Rebirth are excellent places to start. The former is an open-ended RPG with heavily customizable characters, while the latter follows a tightly paced and skillfully curated tale that follows a more linear path. Though very different, both are excellent.How we made this best story games listWhen crafting our list of the best story games, we wanted to offer as diverse a list as possible, showing off the breadth of narrative techniques available across the video game landscape. It was also important to us that older titles be considered, given the strong influence of timeless classics like Deus Ex and Mass Effect 2 on modern game writing.Most crucially, however, we sought to build a list full of titles that immerse players, drawing you into their worlds with evocative writing, dynamic world-building, and distinctive characters. Only games that ticked all three of these boxes were considered for our list and, of those, only the very best made the cut.You Might Also Like...Check out our Nintendo Switch 2 reviewOur picks for the best PS5 gamesSee upcoming games for 2025 and beyond! The best story games in 2025 are more than just tall tales. These titles take full advantage of the interactive nature of video games to deliver truly memorable and emotionally stirring narratives.
Like many of the best RPGs (role-playing games) and best single-player games, the best story games pull you into their worlds with well-written characters, carefully calibrated storylines, and gripping set pieces. However, it's worth remembering that great video game storytelling can be found in all sorts of places. While our best story games list is full of RPGs, we've also included some of the best horror games.
Here at TechRadar Gaming, we know how to identify top-tier story games when we see them. Tens of thousands of our collective lives have gone into playing and researching potential hits, all to help you find your next big adventure. Whether you want a sweeping fantasy adventure or a gritty historical drama, we've got you covered. Read on to find out more.
Why you can trust TechRadar We spend hours testing every product or service we review, so you can be sure you're buying the best. Find out more about how we test.
"Ghost of Yotei feels a little like the PS5 exclusive we‚Äôve been waiting for, and a truly great sequel - though not quite a perfect one. Its visceral, bloody combat, wonderful world and map, sense of exploration, and gripping epic tale are true highlights. And while there are a few imperfections, and it really does wear the influence of its predecessor boldly on its sleeve, it's an adventure and landscape to sink hours and hours of enjoyment into." - Rob Dwiar, Techradar Gaming Managing Editor.
Platforms available: PS5 (PS5 Pro Enhanced)
Ghost of Yotei arrives as a PS5 exclusive, and it has a predictably excellent story that follows new protagonist Atsu. She's on the hunt for a group called the Y≈çtei Six, gathering intel by helping out locals and tracking down bounties. This sequel really expands upon the first game, adding in new weapon types and skills, while focusing on open-world exploration.
After the Yotei Six massacres Atsu's family, you'll jump forward in time, as she seeks revenge. There's great sections where you can instantly switch between childhood memories and present day, making use of the PS5's SSD technology. The story is told using cinematic cutscenes, and there's even options to alter the presentation and camera angles. This is a gripping story that's well worth experiencing on PS5.
"Hell Is Us feels like a game that can't quite decide whether it wants to be a soulslike or not, but the result is still a fantastic experience that is compelling and worthy of high praise. The game borrows FromSoft's excellent combat and dark world-building to create a solid action-adventure game with a twisted real-world setting, filled with memorable moments and stunning - if bleak - vistas. I just wish there was a little more substance; a lack of weapon and enemy variety, plus an all-too-short finale, hold it back from true greatness." - Christian Guyton, TechRadar Gaming reviewer.
Platforms available: PS5 (PS5 Pro Enhanced), Xbox Series X|S, PC
Hell Is Us is extremely devoted to being exactly the kind of game it sets out to be. There's no map, no mini-map, and an overwhelming bleakness to its world that's to be commended. You'll explore the war-torn land of Hadea, which is in the middle of an invasion by mysterious demon creatures, and a Civil War. The history of Hadea's core conflict go back centuries, and its citizens carry the weight of generations of hatred, racism, and military law.
In essence, Hell Is Us plays like a soulslike, but it's also a story-heavy exploration game that rewards player intuition. You'll speak to locals, gather clues and rumors about each locale, and then piece together a path forward. The plot is front and center here, and it's one that covers some seriously challenging subject matter. Hell Is Us is a one-of-a-kind experience that ask a lot from players, but rewards them with a truly detailed world to dive into.
"Death Stranding 2: On the Beach is a great example of a sequel that expands on the original without losing sight of it. The traversal is still the star of the show, while the action has been significantly improved without taking over the experience. While a conventional plot takes the back seat for a more character-driven story, the new cast of characters and a phenomenal final third act stick the landing with prime Hideo Kojima bombast." - Scott McRae, TechRadar Gaming reviewer.
Death Stranding 2: On the Beach doesn't re-invent the wheel, but does make smart changes to the winning formula of the first game, and as a result is a much more comprehensive experience. You'll set off across Mexico at the start of the story, connecting off-grid locations to the Chiral Network, much like the first game. Things quickly take a turn for the worse, however, and Sam is left to pick up the pieces, before setting out on a new adventure.
By switching the main setting to Australia, Death Stranding 2 is quite visually distinct from its predecessor. Sandy dunes and sun-scorched desert are brought to life thanks to dynamic weather and particle effects. This is easily one of the best looking games of the current generation so far, one that contains all of the unique art direction we've come to expect from Kojima Productions. The story is a smaller, more character-focused affair, packing way more emotional punch than we expected. This is easily Kojima's best story so far, and one that's a must play for PS5 players.
"Channeling true JRPG excellence while putting its own western twist on the genre and turn-based combat, Clair Obscur: Expedition 33 is an absolutely belting game. It has exquisite writing and story craft, wonderfully stylish and multifaceted combat, and is a blisteringly beautiful assault on all the senses from top-notch voice acting and audio to some of the most beautiful environments I‚Äôve seen in years. It has the scope and execution of a game built by hundreds of developers, not a few dozen, and is easily an early game of the year contender." - Rob Dwiar, TechRadar Gaming reviewer.
Platforms available: PS5, Xbox Series X|S, and PC
Clair Obscur: Expedition is an instant modern classic, simultaneously paying loving homage to classic JRPs while subverting tropes in favor of innovation. The story is a sprawling epic, featuring performances from a star-studded cast. There's Final Fantasy 16's Ben Starr, Baldur's Gate 3's Jennifer English, Daredevil's Charlie Cox, and The Lord of the Rings' Andy Serkis.
Vibrant world design grabs your attention immediately, as you set off an expedition alongside a crew of beautifully-realized companions. Visually, Clair Obscur: Expedition 33 is easily one of the best looking games we've ever played, backed up by a unique art direction inspired by French art history and architectural principles. Fans of the grand and sometimes operatically-inclined plots of classic JRPGs will find plenty to love here, though these classic leanings are intertwined with dark, relatively grounded twists. For fans of Final Fantasy, Suikoden, Chrono Trigger, and DragonQuest.
"Like a Dragon: Infinite Wealth is a special game with an enthralling narrative that expertly weaves its new characters and plot points with the series‚Äô past. It‚Äôs a story that‚Äôs as thrilling and intense as it is heartwarming and - occasionally - genuinely hilarious." - Cat Bussell, TechRadar Gaming reviewer.
Platforms available: PS5, PS4, Xbox Series X|S, XBO, and PC
Like a Dragon: Infinite Wealth continues the story of new series protagonist Ichiban Kasuga, as he heads to Hawaii in search of his Mother. What makes this games story so special is how it weaves into the previous Yakuza games, bringing Kiryu back for another adventure. This time around, Kiryu is older, wiser, and somehow even more deadly, complimenting Ichiban's hopeful optimism and overall good vibes perfectly.
For fans of the series, there's plenty of throwbacks and cameos to enjoy here, but even better is the way Infinite Wealth manages to tie old plot lines into new ones, setting the scene for future titles, and rewarding those that have stuck around thus far. The main story is equal parts heartwarming, gripping and intense, managing to present the absolute best the series has to offer so far.
"Assassin‚Äôs Creed Shadows is a massive success and a winning combination of stealth and steel. It‚Äôs a fantastic entry in the open-world RPG line of games in the stealth series and the most refined version of that style yet, with satisfying and rewarding exploration, brilliant combat, and a dual protagonist system that really works. Even a few minor quibbles can‚Äôt hold it back." - Rob Dwiar, TechRadar Gaming reviewer.
Platforms available: PS5, Xbox Series X|S, Mac, and PC
Assassin's Creed Shadows finally takes players to Japan, a setting that's been long-requested since the very start of the series. In this iteration, we follow Naoe and Yasuke, as their fates intertwine and send them off on a blood-soaked journey of revenge. Of course, Assassin's Creed Shadows is the latest in the modern RPG version of the series, and as such it focuses on open-world exploration. In many ways, the open world exhibited here is the best Ubisoft has ever put together, managing to look truly impressive in action.
Whether you want to play it sneaky with Naoe, or bust through doors with Yasuke, there's combat here that caters to a wide variety of play styles. Many of the series' hallmarks, like Synchronization points, have been retooled, while others, like social stealth and Leaps of Faith are left largely untouched. This'll no doubt please longtime fans, while giving new ones a great place to jump in. Jumping between dual protagonists, Assassin's Creed Shadows' story is truly epic, backed up by some excellent side missions and quests.
"Lost Records: Bloom & Rage digs deep into the realities of coming of age in the 90s. Whether through snappy, gorgeously rendered cutscenes, fuzzy homemade VHS tapes, or confused conversations at the local watering hole, it‚Äôs a thoughtful story that delivers sincerity in a way that feels quintessentially human. Propped up by a cavalcade of multi-faceted characters, Lost Records: Bloom & Rage Part 1 is a no-holds-barred opening act that will leave you desperate for Part 2." - Sarah Thwaites, TechRadar Gaming reviewer.
Lost Records: Bloom & Rage is a new IP that explores the uncanny, messy nature of humanity from a stylized and period-specific perspective. So far, it‚Äôs an adventure dripping in tactile nostalgia and pithy mystery that evolves the ethos of the games that came before it. Evoking Life is Strange‚Äôs episodic approach, Lost Records: Bloom and Rage is split into two parts, with the second tape coming in April 2025.
In Lost Records: Bloom & Rage Tape 1, four friends who vowed never to speak after an undisclosed incident are summoned back to their hometown when an ominous package arrives in the mail. You play as Swann, an anxious forty-something who must face the events of the troupe‚Äôs ‚Äòlost summer‚Äô, rekindling their dormant relationships to understand why the parcel arrived after all this time and what could be inside. so far, it's an excellent story, one that's well worth jumping into and following as the episodes come out.
"Indiana Jones and the Great Circle has all the components of a thrilling adventure ripped straight from the silver screen. Its global locations are intricately detailed and a joy to explore (despite suffering from lackluster visuals on Xbox Series S) with secrets hidden around every corner while the combat system is developer MachineGames at its best." - Dashiell Wood, TechRadar Gaming reviewer.
Indiana Jones and the Great Circle tells an epic globe-trotting tale that ends up as a shining example of the long-running franchise. In fact, it's the best Indiana Jones story since Indiana Jones and the Last Crusade, thanks largely to an excellent performance from Troy Baker. There's a dastardly villain, some familiar side characters, and plenty of twists and turns, all complimented by some truly fun, whip-cracking action.
Don't go in expecting Indiana Jones and the Great Circle to be an action-heavy FPS affair, as it shares much more with immersive sims like Thief and Dishonored. It's an Indiana Jones simulator, allowing you to experience the world as Indy, as you solve puzzles, punch Nazis, and document the historical wonders that you find along the way.
"Each companion‚Äôs personal storyline is a coherent multi-part adventure, composed of dramatic set-piece battles, gripping dialogue, and gentle walk-and-talk scenes framed against Veilguard‚Äôs jaw-dropping environments. Having a gut-wrenching discussion about family trauma is one thing, but doing so on a sprawling, torchlit coastline at dusk elevates the scene to new heights." - Cat Bussell, TechRadar Gaming reviewer.
After a long tine away, BioWare returns with Dragon Age: The Veilguard, a colourful and genuinely epic action RPG that more than lives up to the legacy of its predecessor's. You play Rook, a character that you'll get to customise and design, picking a class that'll determine your play-style. Combat has been completely overhauled, and decidedly modernized, peppered with pitch-perfect parrying, flashy abilities and explosive team-up moves.
Whether you're a newcomer to the series, or if you've been playing since the very beginning, Dragon Age: The Veilguard's story has plenty to offer, as you and your crew attempt to thwart the evil plans of Solas the Dreadwolf. Along the way you'll meet new friends, make difficult choices, and maybe even fall in love.
"The Quarry excels at what developer Supermassive does best. Fun characters that are brilliantly acted, a branching narrative that loves to twist the knife and top-shelf visuals make for a game that‚Äôs unstoppably thrilling from start to finish." - Rhys Wood, TechRadar Gaming reviewer.
From the masters of interactive horror Supermassive Games comes The Quarry, a visually stunning and rip-roaring rollercoaster of a game that features some of the best motion-capture acting in the. business. David Arquette, Ariel Winter and Justice Smith deliver excellent performances as wayward teens trapped in a nightmarish situation where murderous creatures and dating troubles combine.
Thanks to a wide suite of modes, you can play The Quarry alongside friends, passing the controller, or voting on key decisions. There's a great story to enjoy that pulls from the likes of Scream, Texas Chainsaw Massacre and Evil Dead to create a familiar but frightening mix. You'll want to try this one out on the Xbox Series X, as the lighting effects and facial animation really are spectacular.
Star Wars Jedi: Survivor continues the story set out by its predecessor, building on Cal Kestis, and his crew mates. The result is a compelling tale filled with twists, turns and some truly epic reveals. This is all paired with an expanded lightsaber suite, and a new set of Force abilities to play around with.
Star Wars Jedi: Survivor manages to deliver on its promise of expanding the world of Cal Kestis beyond the events of Fallen Order. At the beginning of Survivor, we find the team somewhat scattered, as Cal sets off on a mission to rekindle the Jedi order, and save other Force-sensitive individuals. Along the way, you'll meet some familiar faces, and some wonderful new ones, hopping from planet to planet while evading the Empire.
What Star Wars Jedi: Survivor excels at is telling a much larger story when compared to its predecessor. There's more characters, way more twists and turns, and some great reveals that tie into the wider Star Wars universe. Pair this with excellent lightsaber combat and even a semi-open world planet and you've got a very good time indeed.
"Building upon the themes of its predecessor, God of War Ragnarok‚Äôs emotive narrative shines in its subtler moments, while clever evolutions to combat introduce welcome changes that advance gameplay without oversaturating it. It‚Äôs a sequel that is often as brutal as it is poignant ‚Äì and a fitting next chapter in Kratos and Atreus‚Äô journey." - Vic Hood, TechRadar Gaming reviewer.
God of War Ragnarok takes what made its predecessor so epic, and dials it up to eleven. The combat has been refined, adding in shield-focused abilities and skills, and traversal has been improved thanks to a bunch of genuinely fun new tools. Kratos and Atreus face down Odin himself in this gargantuan sequel, and must recruit the help of some uneasy allies to get the job done.
There's a great ensemble cast in God of War Ragnarok that helps elevate the story above others in the genre. There's a talking squirrel, more fun from everyone's dismembered head, and plenty of father-son anguish from Kratos and Atreus. The story wraps up Kratos' Norse story rather well, while leaving things open for more adventures later down the line. If you enjoyed the first game, this one is an absolute must play. If you didn't play it, then what are you waiting for!
"Baldur‚Äôs Gate 3 is a fine contender for one of the best video game RPGs ever made. It‚Äôs the most ambitious RPG out there, and the painstakingly accurate rendition of Dungeons & Dragons will delight fans. A must-play, even if some frustrations with D&D‚Äôs format might grate." - Jake Tucker, TechRadar Gaming reviewer.
Platforms available: PS5, Xbox Series X|S and PC
Baldur's Gate 3 offers phenomenal storytelling, more than earning a place on this best story games roundup. Contrary to CRPGs of the past, Baldur's Gate 3 provides a cinematic experience. Every cutscene is expertly voice-acted, with motion capture assisting the voice actors in bringing the game's cast to life. The game also features a narrator whose lavish descriptions are as captivating as they are immersive.
Larian Studios' hit RPG presents you with a multitude of branching paths, all of which feel just as rewarding and legitimate as the others. This allows you to craft a tale that's entirely your own, offering you a fantasy playground that, somehow, retains a strong sense of narrative coherency throughout. Whether you're a goody-two-shoes Paladin or a tyrannical Sorcerer, you can play the game your way - no mean feat for a title of this scale.
"Final Fantasy 7 Rebirth proves that the remake trilogy isn‚Äôt a remake in the strictest sense. However, if you‚Äôre looking to go on another thrilling adventure with Cloud, Tifa, Aerith, Barret, Yuffie, and Red XIII, then you‚Äôve come to the right place - just don‚Äôt expect it to be the adventure you‚Äôre used to." - Cat Bussell, TechRadar Gaming reviewer.
Final Fantasy 7 Rebirth stands as the second installment in the Final Fantasy 7 Remake trilogy. While its predecessor is a gorgeous reimagining of the first act of the 1997 classic, Rebirth goes a step further. This confident, fantastical RPG is jam-packed with meaningful storytelling, unforgettable characters, and plenty of engaging (though never overwhelming) side content.
The story follows Cloud Strife, a traumatized mercenary, who, along with his colorful band of allies, is pursuing a quest to stop the nefarious Sephiroth from ending all life on the planet. Rebirth plays fast and loose with big themes and important ideas, giving its tale a sort of mythological quality The RPG's dramatic, bombastic, and confident cutscenes are punctuated by a fantastic combat system which, though nominally in real-time, allows you to pause and make decisions. Rebirth tells an unforgettable tale, addressing themes of friendship, loyalty, tyranny, love, and identity. It's dense, but, if you're looking for a tale that holds nothing back, then this could be the best story game for you.
The Last of Us Part 1 acts exactly as a remaster should. The improved graphics and mechanics don't come at the expense of the tragic and poignant tale at the game's core. On the contrary, they uplift it, revitalizing the original.
The Last of Us Part 1 is, at the time of writing, the definitive way to experience the tense action sequences and melancholy storytelling that immortalized its original predecessor. Besides graphical improvements and the occasional mechanical tweak, the game remains much as it always has been, providing a gripping post-apocalyptic tale wrapped up in third-person action.
Perhaps more than any other title on this list, The Last of Us Part 1 offers impeccable pacing which is reinforced by game mechanics. Frantic combat setpieces are broken up by slow, pensive moments of scavenging, both of which are, in turn, punctuated by cutscenes that masterfully build dramatic tension. Naughty Dog's tale shows us that the most important thing about the end of the world isn't the disaster itself, but the people living with it.
In Stars and Time subverts your expectations by dropping you in at the end of a fantastical adventure rather than at the start. As soon as you begin, you'll find yourself waist-deep in the established relationships between colorful characters, immersing you head-first in the moving story.
Platforms available: PS5, PS4, Nintendo Switch, and PC
With roots in classic turn-based RPGs of yore and modern indie triumphs like Undertale, In Stars and Time takes a bold approach towards storytelling which breaks the mold established by many of the best story games on this list. In a manner reminiscent of Deathloop, protagonist Siffrin finds themself trapped in a time loop as they fight to defeat the apocalyptic schemes of the sinister King.
The writing sparkles and delights, gradually raising the game's emotional stakes until you find yourself fully invested in its characters. As you loop around again and again, you'll begin to share Siffrin's frustration with their situation. While, on paper, tasks might become repetitive, the very act of repetition pulls you deeper into the story, making for a narrative that captivates and challenges all at once.
"Alan Wake 2 stands out as a champion among modern survival horror games. Its beautifully woven story encompasses everything you could want from a blockbuster horror title. Expertly crafted cutscenes meld together reality and video games while thrilling combat and frightening chases keep things interesting as you dig into a gripping narrative." - Ellie Gould, TechRadar Gaming reviewer.
Platforms available: PS5, Xbox Series X|S, PC
Alan Wake 2 scared and thrilled us in equal measure, setting a new bar for modern survival horror titles. Its compelling storyline is full of twists and turns, more than doing justice to the Stephen King novels that inspired it. From Remedy Entertainment, the third-person horror title embroils you in increasingly unsettling supernatural events, blurring conventional narrative boundaries with all sorts of twists and tricks. Though its predecessor is an excellent psychological horror game, it isn't necessary to play the first game to understand the second, as the more recent title is built with newer players in mind.The story follows the twin perspectives of FBI Agent Saga Anderson and Alan Wake himself as they try to survive the supernatural threats that beset them. The grim tale burrows into your brain, luring you in with tantalizing and shocking mysteries until you're completely immersed in the morbidly fascinating game world. Staff Writer Elie Gould called Alan Wake 2 "beautifully terrifying" in their review for TRG. "I also couldn't ever put it down, despite its scares giving me the shakes."
Deus Ex is, in many respects, a parent to modern immersive sims. Additionally, it offers a cyberpunk story that wrestles with difficult questions about globalization, transhumanism, and political ideology.
Released in the year 2000, many of the entries on this best story games list owe a great deal to the innovations made in the original Deus Ex. Developed by Ion Storm, this sci-fi RPG has you take on the role of JC Denton, an agent of the United Nations Anti-Terrorist Coalition. Like its spiritual successors Deus Ex: Human Revolution and Deus Ex: Mankind Divided, the title addresses themes of transhumanism by having its protagonist augmented with superpower-granting nanomachines.
As well as offering a well-paced main storyline, Deus Ex allows the player to tell their own story by completing objectives their own way. Stealth, conversation, and brute force are all tools in your arsenal, to be used whenever and however you see fit. Even the ending, which we won't spoil, offers tremendous scope for player choice, forcing you to put your moral code on the line as you determine the fate of the world.
Cyberpunk 2077 immerses you in the murky moral problems of Night City, dragging you down into the sump and challenging your beliefs with plenty of difficult choices. The Phantom Liberty expansion is a particular treat in this way, and still keeps me up at night.
Platforms available: PS5, PS4, Xbox Series X|S, Xbox One, and PC
Thanks to the much-celebrated Patch 2.0 update, Cyberpunk 2077 has come into its own, ensuring that bugs and clunky mechanics no longer get in the way of storytelling by doing away with both. It may be over three years since sci-fi RPG's launch, but CD Projekt Red's dark cyberpunk tale now stands on its own feet, earning a well-deserved place on our list of the best story games.
With memorable characters and more than a few shocking twists, Cyberpunk 2077 offers a relatively linear story, but still squeezes in ample opportunities to confront you with difficult moral choices that roll on to affect the narrative. Despite this linearity, the story is powerful and confronts important themes themes both personal and political.
In terms of sheer spectacle, few games can go toe to toe with this Spidey sequel. Venom is the standout star, as he jumps back and forth between characters, forcing them to battle it out as a dangerous plot unfolds. It builds on everything the first game, and its spin-off laid down, culminating in one of gaming's best stories.
Marvel's Spider-Man 2 picks up with Miles Morales and Peter Parker, as they swing from building to building to stop a gargantuan threat against the city. From the get-go, the sheer scale of the game impresses, and continues to wow right up until the credits. It's arguably the best story you can play on PS5, one that ties together threads from the previous two games, while promising big things to come.
The main story of Marvel's Spider-Man 2 focuses on Peter Parker, who, after an encounter with the Venom symbiote, gains new abilities and a heightened sense of power. This is, of course, a familiar Spider-Man tale, but there's some clever twists and turns along the way here to keep things fresh and interesting. Namely, in the involvement of Harry Osbourne, and of course a second Spider-Man in Miles Morales. Miles' story in particular, is a heartfelt one about how revenge always comes at a cost, with excellent performances all around.
Sony exclusives are known for their larger than life stories, and Marvel's Spider-Man 2 is no exception. Thrilling villains, huge set-pieces and Easter Eggs galore make this one absolutely essential if you have a PS5.
Red Dead Redemption 2 is as immersive as they come. Emulating the glacial pacing of westerns like Deadwood and Django Unchained, Rockstar Games' historical epic rewards patience and tenacity, offering a resonant story that slowly but steadily draws you into the game's world.
The best story game of its kind, Red Dead Redemption 2 is an immersive, narrative-driven third-person action game that presents a detailed and complex portrait of a gang of outlaws as they roam what remains of the Wild West - always hoping to stay one step ahead of the law. There is a deep romance to the title, which simultaneously lionizes the rugged individualism of the cowboy lifestyle while, in the same breath, challenging the notion that such a way of life could ever have existed.
Though Red Dead Redemption 2 doesn't tell a particularly original story, the way it spins its yarn of choice is absolutely breathtaking, commanding the player's full attention with well-paced narrative beats and surprising plot twists to keep you on your toes. As you play, you will find that the gang's triumphs and failures begin to feel like your own; a testament to the warmth and empathy that runs through the game's heart.
Mass Effect 2 has one of the most memorable and distinctive ensemble casts in video game history. All 12 of the supporting characters have rich backstories, and, thanks to the range of dialogue options, you're able to feel a sense of ownership over your protagonist's relationships with their crew.
Platforms available: PS5, PS4, Xbox Series X|S, Xbox One and PC
The crowning jewel of the Mass Effect saga, Mass Effect 2 brings some much-needed sci-fi drama to our best story games list. Though all three entries in the core saga are fantastic titles in their own right, Mass Effect 2 stands apart, offering both the best standalone experience and the strongest story arc of the three. As you progress through the tale, you'll need to make difficult choices, weighing up challenging moral dilemmas throughout BioWare's epic space opera.
In this third-person RPG, Commander Shepard has to save the galaxy from an ancient threat. No longer backed by the galactic government, they have turned to a dubious terrorist organization for funding and support. Throughout the game, you'll be gearing up for the 'suicide mission', a daring assault on the enemy's base of operations where the main characters, including your protagonist, can perish. To this end, you'll need to assemble a crew, upgrade your ship, and prepare for the fight of a lifetime. In the process, your Shepard will forge new relationships, tackle new hardships, and, possibly, even fall in love.
Alan Wake 2 undoubtedly has an exceptional storyline. However, the answer to this question is very much dependent on a player's individual tastes. Any of the games on our best story games list could qualify depending on your taste in genre and storytelling style. If you're a fan of more realistic tales, you're more likely to get a kick out of Red Dead Redemption 2 than the more fanciful Baldur's Gate 3. That being said, sometimes stepping out of your comfort zone can be rewarding, as you may discover a brand-new type of game that you may never have considered before. For instance, though Deus Ex may be unfamiliar to many on account of its age, the sci-fi classic is well worth a look.

That being said, sometimes stepping out of your comfort zone can be rewarding, as you may discover a brand-new type of game that you may never have considered before. For instance, though Deus Ex may be unfamiliar to many on account of its age, the sci-fi classic is well worth a look.
Between Clair Obscur: Expedition 33 and Assassin's Creed Shadows, story fans are eating well at the moment. However, it's hard to say which story game is the absolute 'best'. Personal taste is a huge factor in determining which games stick with us and, while every title on this best story games list is a masterclass in its own right, we can't rightly say that any one of them stands above the others. That said, if you're interested in seeing how modern game development tackles story games, then the aforementioned Baldur's Gate 3 and Final Fantasy 7 Rebirth are excellent places to start. The former is an open-ended RPG with heavily customizable characters, while the latter follows a tightly paced and skillfully curated tale that follows a more linear path. Though very different, both are excellent.

When crafting our list of the best story games, we wanted to offer as diverse a list as possible, showing off the breadth of narrative techniques available across the video game landscape. It was also important to us that older titles be considered, given the strong influence of timeless classics like Deus Ex and Mass Effect 2 on modern game writing.
Most crucially, however, we sought to build a list full of titles that immerse players, drawing you into their worlds with evocative writing, dynamic world-building, and distinctive characters. Only games that ticked all three of these boxes were considered for our list and, of those, only the very best made the cut.

Storytelling in video games has evolved dramatically in recent years, and in 2025, narrative-rich PC titles are delivering emotional depth, player-driven decision-making, and cinematic quality rivaling Hollywood films. From surreal puzzle adventures to dystopian RPGs, these games aren‚Äôt just about gameplay‚Äîthey‚Äôre experiences that stay with you long after the credits roll. What makes a great story game? It‚Äôs not just plot‚Äîit‚Äôs characters you care about, choices that matter, and themes that challenge your perspective. And thanks to advances in AI, voice acting, and branching dialogue systems, modern story-driven games now offer an unparalleled level of immersion. Whether you‚Äôre into dark philosophical explorations or heartfelt emotional journeys, here are the most compelling narrative PC games you should be playing in 2025: Top Story-Rich PC Games in 2025 1. Black Myth: Wukong Black Myth Wukong Genre: Action RPG Why It Stands Out: A mythological epic blending Souls-like combat with deep Chinese folklore. Story Highlights: You play as the Destined One, battling gods and demons across surreal landscapes inspired by Journey to the West. The game explores themes of destiny, enlightenment, and sacrifice. Fun Fact: It became one of the fastest-selling PC titles of 2024, drawing comparisons to Elden Ring for its scale and story execution. 2. Metaphor: ReFantazio Genre: Fantasy RPG Why It Stands Out: From the creators of Persona 5, this is a political allegory set in a vibrant medieval world. Story Highlights: A battle for the throne turns into a meditation on identity and fear. Dialogue choices shape political alliances and character fates. 3. Clair Obscur: Expedition 33 Genre: Turn-based RPG Why It Stands Out: One of the most stylistically daring RPGs of the year, blending poetry and tragedy in a painterly world. Story Highlights: A dying society‚Äôs final hope rests on a cursed expedition. The game‚Äôs melancholy tone explores grief, legacy, and the price of progress. 4. Citizen Sleeper 2 Genre: Sci-fi Narrative RPG Why It Stands Out: Like its predecessor, this sequel offers choice-driven survival mechanics and a cyberpunk dystopia. Story Highlights: You play as a synthetic human navigating a morally gray world. Every decision alters your relationships and survival chances, with multiple endings shaped by your path. 5. The Drifter Genre: Horror Adventure Why It Stands Out: A gritty, psychological thriller that evokes the tension of Black Mirror and Twin Peaks. Story Highlights: A man mysteriously resurrected from death uncovers a twisted conspiracy. Dialogue and exploration push the story forward in a classic point-and-click format. 6. Tell Me Why (Free on Steam until July 1, 2025) Genre: Narrative Adventure Why It Stands Out: One of the few mainstream games with a transgender protagonist, created with authentic input from LGBTQ+ consultants. Story Highlights: Twins revisit their childhood home in Alaska, uncovering the truth behind a traumatic event. Empathy, memory, and sibling bonds drive the narrative. 7. Life Is Strange: Double Exposure Genre: Supernatural Mystery Adventure Why It Stands Out: Max Caulfield returns, now grappling with multiverse timelines to solve a murder. Story Highlights: The game deepens its signature emotional storytelling with parallel-world mechanics, making each choice echo across realities. 8. Silent Hill 2 Remake Genre: Survival Horror Why It Stands Out: A reimagining of one of gaming‚Äôs greatest psychological horror tales. Story Highlights: James Sunderland returns to the foggy town searching for his dead wife, encountering surreal horrors that reflect his inner guilt. Faithful to the original‚Äôs narrative depth but rebuilt with Unreal Engine 5 for modern hardware. 9. Blue Prince Genre: Puzzle Adventure Why It Stands Out: This indie gem is a mystery box of shifting architecture, secrets, and atmosphere. Story Highlights: Players explore a sentient, ever-changing mansion while unraveling a cryptic narrative through environmental storytelling and logic puzzles. 10. Before Your Eyes Genre: Interactive Drama Why It Stands Out: A rare title that uses real-world blinking to progress its story. Story Highlights: The game traces a life from childhood to death, with every blink representing time passing. It‚Äôs a meditative and heart-wrenching journey about how we remember our lives. Why Story Games Are Flourishing on PC in 2025 PC remains the ideal platform for narrative games, thanks to: Wider indie support: Games like Blue Prince and The Drifter thrive through Steam and Itch.io. Modding and accessibility tools: Titles like Citizen Sleeper 2 feature fan-driven expansions and localization mods. Advanced hardware support: RTX graphics cards and AI-powered upscaling bring cinematic fidelity to even low-budget indie stories. Whether you want branching choices, character-driven arcs, or innovative mechanics like eye-tracking or real-time memory systems, PC gaming in 2025 offers an unmatched storytelling playground. And with anticipated titles like The Wolf Among Us 2 and Dustborn still on the horizon, this trend shows no signs of slowing. Pro Tip: If you‚Äôre new to narrative games, start with Tell Me Why while it‚Äôs free, then dive into Life Is Strange: Double Exposure or Clair Obscur for deeper, more experimental stories. Key Takeaways Story-driven PC games combine engaging gameplay with rich narratives Player choices often shape the plot in interactive storytelling experiences Top story games span various genres and offer deep character development Defining Story-Driven PC Games Story-driven PC games put the plot front and center. These games focus on deep tales that pull players in and keep them hooked. Role-Playing Games and Their Narratives RPGs often have the most complex stories in gaming. Games like ‚ÄúThe Witcher 3: Wild Hunt‚Äù and ‚ÄúMass Effect 2‚Äù let players shape the story. They offer big worlds to explore and lots of quests. Players can make choices that change how the story ends. In RPGs, characters grow and change as the story moves on. Players often spend many hours getting to know the game‚Äôs heroes. This helps them care more about what happens in the story. Some RPGs use a mix of text and voice acting to tell their tales. Others rely more on player choice to build the story. Adventure and Interactive Storytelling Adventure games focus on puzzle-solving and story. They often have less action than RPGs. Games like ‚ÄúThe Walking Dead‚Äù and ‚ÄúWhat Remains of Edith Finch‚Äù are good examples. These games often use point-and-click controls. Players explore scenes and talk to characters to move the story forward. Some adventure games are like movies you can play. Visual novels are a type of adventure game with lots of reading. They show static scenes with text and sometimes voice acting. Players make choices that change the story‚Äôs path. Horror Games: A Blend of Fear and Storyline Horror games mix scary moments with deep stories. They often deal with dark themes and hard choices. Games like ‚ÄúSOMA‚Äù use fear to make players think about big ideas. These games can have jump scares, but the best ones build a sense of dread. They use sound and visuals to create a spooky mood. The story often revolves around solving a mystery or staying alive. Some horror games let players fight back against monsters. Others focus more on running and hiding. The story in horror games often has twists that keep players guessing until the end. Outstanding Examples of Story-Driven Games Story-driven games transport players to rich worlds filled with complex characters and gripping plots. These games span genres and platforms, offering memorable experiences through their narratives. Epic Sagas and Open Worlds Baldur‚Äôs Gate 3 takes players on a grand fantasy adventure. This role-playing game features deep character development and player choice. The world reacts to decisions, creating a unique story for each player. Red Dead Redemption 2 brings the Wild West to life. Players explore a vast open world as outlaw Arthur Morgan. The game‚Äôs story deals with themes of loyalty, redemption, and the end of an era. God of War and its sequel God of War Ragnarok reimagine the series. They follow Kratos and his son on an emotional journey through Norse mythology. The games blend action with a touching father-son story. The Witcher 3: Wild Hunt stars Geralt of Rivia, a monster hunter for hire. Players roam a massive fantasy world, making choices that shape the story. Side quests are as rich and engaging as the main plot. Indie Gems and Innovative Storytelling Undertale subverts role-playing game tropes with its unique combat system. Players can choose to fight monsters or befriend them. Each choice affects the story, leading to multiple endings. Disco Elysium puts players in the shoes of a detective with amnesia. The game focuses on dialogue and skill checks rather than combat. It tackles complex themes like politics and identity. Night in the Woods tells the story of Mae, a college dropout who returns to her hometown. The game explores themes of mental health and economic struggles. Its quirky art style pairs well with its heartfelt narrative. Narrative-Driven Games Across Platforms Story-rich games are not limited to PCs. Many are available on consoles like Xbox One and PlayStation. Some have even made their way to mobile platforms. The Walking Dead series by Telltale Games brought interactive storytelling to iOS and Android. Players make tough choices that affect the story‚Äôs outcome. Life is Strange is playable on PC, consoles, and mobile devices. It follows Max, a student who can rewind time. The game deals with friendship, time travel, and the consequences of choices. What Remains of Edith Finch, available on Switch and other platforms, tells the stories of a cursed family. Players explore the family home, uncovering tales of each family member‚Äôs fate.
